(London) Certain quarters here stated today that the American delegation to the naval preparatory conference will return to the United States aboard the mail ship Washington, which is scheduled to set sail on December 29th. According to another reliable source, the British government has decided to propose that preparatory negotiations be resumed in March next year. It is learned that Japan will agree to the British proposal, while the United States will only agree if Japan proposes a new disarmament plan before the resumption of talks. (Eleventh National Telegram)

(London) Through repeated meetings between Britain, Japan, and the United States during the naval preparatory talks, the Japanese delegation has completed discussions on all issues within the scope of the government's instructions. On the eleventh, a telegram was sent to the home government requesting instructions regarding the attitude to be taken in the future. The important points of its content are as follows: (1) To settle the results of all past talks, whether to restart negotiations after Japan declares the abolition of the Washington Treaty; (2) Or to continue the talks in the current state;

(3) Whether to proceed with more concrete matters. If the government adopts the third approach, it will be necessary to discuss the issue of maximum warship construction numbers. (Eleventh Japan United Press Dispatch)

(London) Representatives Matsudaira and Yamamoto stated in talks that the Japanese delegation recently exchanged views with British and American representatives on technical issues. As a result, the views of the United Kingdom and the United States on specialized matters are clear. Therefore, they reported all the details to their home government.

At the same time, they requested instructions from the government on what policy to adopt to break the current stalemate. (Eleventh Japan United Press Dispatch)

Japan Prepares to Notify Abolition of Naval Treaty 53

But Still Hopes Meetings Will Continue

(Tokyo) The Japanese government's proposal to abolish the Washington Treaty passed the Privy Council's review committee on the eleventh and will be formally decided at the Privy Council's plenary meeting on the nineteenth. On the twenty-second, the Cabinet will add the statement "Announce the abolition of the treaty based on the clear text of Article 23 of the Washington Treaty" to the document, which will then be sent to Ambassador Saito in the United States and submitted to the American government. At the same time, the Japanese government will issue a statement announcing the reasons and its beliefs. (Twelfth Japan United Press Dispatch)

(Tokyo) During the Privy Council review committee meeting on the eleventh, the following questions were raised regarding the issue of naval arms race:

A Privy Council member asked: After Japan abandons the treaty, if a new treaty cannot be established, will Japan and the United Kingdom and the United States not engage in a naval arms race?

The government representative replied: Japan has no intention of actively engaging in a naval arms race. The United Kingdom and the United States also seem to have the same view. The government intends to repeatedly initiate necessary negotiations to achieve its goals. However, because it is difficult to guarantee that a naval arms race will absolutely not occur, sufficient countermeasures have been considered. If the United Kingdom and the United States provoke competition with Japan, Japan is prepared to respond to the competition based on its national conditions and economic situation. Japan adopts the fundamental principle of not threatening or invading other countries, and builds submarines and other warships based on the doctrine of being sufficient for defense but not enough to attack other countries. There is no need to worry about the occurrence of a naval arms race. A Privy Council member asked: What about the Pacific defense agreement after the treaty is abandoned?

The government representative replied: Japan hopes to retain its agreement, but if other countries do not wish to, it cannot be helped.

A Privy Council member asked: What if the United Kingdom and the United States request an extension of the meeting period?

The government representative replied: The timing of the disarmament conference is clearly stipulated in both the Washington and London treaties. The Japanese government naturally advocates holding the meeting as scheduled next year. (Twelfth Japan United Press Dispatch)

(Tokyo) It is heard that Japan, in principle, is willing to continue the current London naval talks and does not object to the rumored British proposal to postpone the meeting for three months. If the United Kingdom does so before the end of this week, the action will be earlier than Japan's abolition of the Washington Naval Convention. (Twelfth Reuters Dispatch)

Recently, when I traveled to the United States, I had conversations with various people and deeply felt that American feelings towards the United Kingdom have gradually increased. U.S. Army Department Sells Munitions to Japan 56

160,000 Rounds of Ammunition Handled by the Heng Hsin Yanghang Ten Years Ago

New Discoveries in Senate Investigation Continue

(Washington) When the Senate Committee Investigating the Arms Trade reopened its hearings today, it discovered that in 1922, the Heng Hsin Yanghang (i.e., DuPont Company) had agreed with the Army Department to sell 160,000 rounds of ammunition in the Army's possession to Japan. There is a letter in the Heng Hsin Yanghang's files stating that although selling Army ammunition to foreigners is not an appropriate procedure, it does not violate Army regulations, etc. Heng Hsin Yanghang officials stated that since the Army Department knew that Japan could purchase such munitions from the United Kingdom, it was happy to assist American manufacturers. The Investigating Committee also found a letter from the Heng Hsin Yanghang in 1932 stating that American merchants selling military supplies to the Japanese Navy Department was considered not only permissible but also feasible, as the Navy Department was very willing to know the quantity and nature of munitions purchased by Japan. If Japan procured them in Europe, such information would be impossible to know. (Eleventh Reuters Dispatch)

League of Nations Resolves Important Cases, Affecting Next Year's Overall Situation 57

Soviet Representative Appointed Assistant Secretary of the League of Nations

Prague Czech Foreign Minister Dr. Beneš told a guest today that the recent deliberations of the League of Nations Administrative Council will have a very good impact on international politics in 1935. The League of Nations has properly resolved far-reaching issues such as the Saar issue and the dispute between Southern Hungary. We can be truly satisfied. We have defeated those who advocate revising the peace treaty. (Eleventh Reuters Dispatch)

(Geneva) The eighty-third session of the League of Nations Administrative Council held its final meeting today. Italian Representative Aloisi presented a report on the procedures for the international police force to enter the Saar during the Saar plebiscite, which was unanimously approved. The costs of accommodation and supplies for this police force will be paid from the plebiscite funds. When the funds are insufficient, Germany and France will be asked to bear them separately. However, under no circumstances shall the assets and income of the League of Nations itself be used for the Saar issue. All police forces shall enjoy extraterritorial rights during their service in the Saar, and all criminal cases committed by these police forces shall be handled by the Supreme Plebiscite Tribunal. Afterwards, the chairman, Czech Representative Beneš, delivered a closing speech, stating that the next session of the Administrative Council has been changed from January 21st to January 11th next year, advanced by ten days to deal with various issues related to the Saar plebiscite. Before today's final meeting, the Administrative Council held a closed-door meeting and elected Mr. Rosenberg, the Soviet Chargé d'affaires in France, as the Deputy Secretary-General of the League of Nations. However, he will not be assigned a substantive position at present and will only serve as an extra staff member. It is reported that the Soviet Union had requested the appointment of a Russian as the Director of the Political Section, but a British person currently holds that position. The British government opposed this matter, so this position was added to appease the Soviet Union. (Eleventh National Telegram)

(London) According to an announcement by the War Office today, Lieutenant General Byng has been appointed as the Commander-in-Chief of the international police force maintaining order during the Saar plebiscite. Lieutenant General Byng is currently the Commander of the Fourth Division of the British Army and participated in the South African War and the European War. In addition to receiving the British honor, Italy, France, and Portugal also praised his military achievements. (Eleventh Reuters Dispatch)

(London) The two British police teams sent to the Saar region will depart from the United Kingdom on Sunday and next Tuesday, traveling via Dover and Calais. They will be transported free of charge through France. British Major General Hylton heads the International Police Command. Hylton is currently consulting with War Office authorities on security matters. Hylton is 56 years old and served on the General Staff during the Great War. He has just returned to London from India, where he had been stationed for a long time. (Twelfth National Telegram)

(Geneva) Current Soviet Chargé d'affaires in France, Mr. Rubinin, was recently elected as an assistant secretary of the League of Nations by the non-public meeting of the League of Nations Executive Council. The League of Nations Secretariat currently has one Secretary-General, namely the Frenchman Avenol, two Deputy Secretaries-General, namely the Spaniard Azcarate and the Italian Pilotti, and three Assistant Secretaries, one being the Englishman Walters, one German, and one Japanese. After Germany and Japan withdrew from the League of Nations, the two vacant seats are now filled by the Soviet Union to supplement one seat. (Eleventh Havas Dispatch)

Magnificent Grand Hotel Destroyed by Fire 61

Entire Building Reduced to Ashes

Many Guests Were State Legislators

More Than Forty Buried in the Flames

Lansing, Michigan The Koons Hotel here, located next to the Grand River, is very luxurious and accommodates approximately two hundred guests, most of whom are members of the state legislature, as the state legislature is in session. Before dawn this morning, the hotel suddenly caught fire, and the entire building was reduced to ashes. It has been ascertained that approximately one hundred guests escaped. About forty people died, including five legislators. The rest are missing, so the exact number of deaths will not be known until the rubble is dug up tomorrow. When the fire was raging, many guests jumped into the river, some of whom drowned, while others, wearing only their nightclothes, braved the cold and sought refuge in the snow-covered streets. As for those who fell from the building and were injured, there were also many. (Eleventh Reuters Dispatch)

Lansing The number of deaths caused by the Koons Hotel fire cannot be ascertained, but it is now known that fourteen people have died, seventy are missing, and twenty-nine are injured. When the fire was raging, some people took refuge on the roof, but unexpectedly the roof collapsed, and all were buried in the flames. One servant repeatedly risked his life, running along the corridors and knocking on doors, waking up the sleeping guests, disregarding his own safety to ensure the safety of the guests. This servant's chivalry is truly admirable. (Twelfth Reuters Dispatch)

Cold Wave Lashes United States 62

People Freeze to Death on New York Roads

Chicago Accumulates Ten Inches of Snow

(New York) Recently, floods have occurred in many parts of the country, causing many deaths. Today, a cold wave has lashed the United States, from the East Coast to the West Coast. The temperature in New York is twelve degrees below freezing, and twelve people have frozen to death. It is estimated that there are 10,000 homeless people. Shelters have now been opened here. A shipyard in Somerset, Massachusetts, was destroyed by fire, with losses of approximately $100,000. The central lakes of Maine are thickly frozen to ten inches. Chicago received ten inches of snow today. (Eleventh Reuters Dispatch)

Lisbon The entire country is experiencing heavy rain and strong winds today. Low-lying areas in cities such as Lisbon and Porto have been flooded. All Countries Except Finland Stop Paying War Debts 64

British Reply Delivered to Washington

(Washington) British Ambassador to the United States Sir Ronald Lindsay today delivered a note to Secretary of State Hull, stating that the United Kingdom does not wish to pay the war debt due on Saturday and believes that there is no need to negotiate this matter. The note stated that it is both useless and unwise to negotiate this matter at present, but it will still seek opportunities to resolve this matter. At the same time, the Finnish Minister to the United States also sent a note to the State Department stating that Finland is paying $2,228,000 in war debt due, clearing the semi-annual installment. As for the federal government, it has not sought the opinion of Congress regarding credit payments this year, so the United States does not expect that country to pay. Other European countries have also notified the State Department that they have no intention of paying their debts. (Eleventh National Telegram)

Germany Abandons Policy of Concentrating Shipping 65

Restores Independent Operation of Companies

(Berlin) Germany has been implementing a policy of concentrating shipping since 1930. The authorities are very dissatisfied with the results of this measure and have apparently decided to abandon it and restore independent operation. According to Senator Albert Esbjerg, a leading figure in German shipping, today, the joint operation agreement made by the North German Lloyd and Hapag-Lloyd in 1930, which was to last for fifty years, will be submitted to the government for approval to be abolished and stipulated that Hapag-Lloyd operate: (1) the North Pacific; (2) East Asia and Australia; and (3) Central and South America and the American West Coast lines. North German Lloyd will operate the North Atlantic and Pacific lines. The remaining smaller companies affected by the concentration policy can now all operate independently again. According to Esbjerg's statement today, the concentration policy has not been profitable. The total German tonnage has decreased from 4.2 million tons to 3.4 million tons. The government should still subsidize shipping to compensate for the losses caused by currency fluctuations. (Eleventh Reuters Dispatch)

Arrested Railway Workers Tortured; Soviet Russia Strongly Protests to the Puppet Regime 66

Whipping and Other Inhumane Acts Used

Leading to Crippling or Death

Demanding the Right to Retain Compensation

Blagoveshchensk, Early August of this year, the Soviet Consul-General in Harbin repeatedly lodged written and oral protests with the Manchurian government regarding the arbitrary arrest and abuse of Soviet citizens and the torture of arrested employees of the Chinese Eastern Railway. The "Manchurian Authorities" either ignored these protests or issued general statements (when absolutely necessary), justifying their actions, claiming that the accused had committed serious crimes, and that details would be announced after a preliminary investigation. They also claimed that prisoners were treated normally and not subjected to severe torture.

Subsequently, the world press exposed the "Manchurian" side's abuse of Soviet expatriates, forcing the "Manchurian government" to formally respond to the Soviet Consul-General's protest. On November 6, Shi Lüben, the "Manchurian" special envoy in Harbin, issued a statement that was worded unusually, unlike typical diplomatic documents. Shi forcefully asserted the legality of the "Manchurian" side's actions, stating only that the crimes of the prisoners were "extremely serious in nature and involved a wide range of issues," with "the central issue being the Chinese Eastern Railway." However, he never mentioned the specific crimes committed. Shi denied the use of torture, claiming that the treatment of prisoners "did not exceed normal standards."

On November 26, the Acting Soviet Consul-General in Harbin, Levide, replied that Shi's statement did not satisfactorily address the Soviet Consul-General's requests. Levide stated that Shi's letter did not provide clear answers to specific facts regarding several illegal arrests and violations. Moreover, he did not mention what kind of punishment should be meted out for these illegal actions. The letter only contained general statements expressing the "Manchurian" side's efforts to avoid answering three important key questions regarding the case. Levide reiterated his repeated requests to be informed of the location of the arrested personnel and whether these cases were being tried in court or investigated by administrative authorities, adding that the "Manchurian" side had ignored such requests, and that Shi's statement on November 6 did not address these issues. Shi did not provide a specific answer to the question of what crimes the arrested Soviet citizens had committed, stating only that "the crimes of the prisoners are extremely serious in nature and involve a wide range of issues, and they have been committed more than once." He provided no reasons for this. Such a statement without basis or reason cannot be considered an explanation of the "Manchurian" side's actions. Logically, if the reasons for the arrests were exceptionally serious and the preliminary investigation had lasted two and a half to three months, at least the specific articles and clauses of the criminal law violated should have been ascertained. Therefore, a general statement about the "seriousness of the crimes committed" by 150 Soviet citizens cannot be considered satisfactory. Levide further pointed out that some "Manchurian" authorities were attempting to fabricate charges against Soviet employees of the Chinese Eastern Railway. These false accusations were absurd and had never been proven because they had not committed any crimes.

Levide recalled his repeated protests regarding the severe torture of prisoners and reiterated several new facts, stating, "On September 4, Your Excellency received physical examination certificates regarding prisoners Golovina and Grigoriev, who had been tortured by the Harbin Military Police. On September 14, Vice-Consul Trepinsky showed you the bloodstained underwear of Soviet citizen Ger伏德夫, who was arrested by railway police. His underwear was given to his family by the police. On October 3, the same Vice-Consul informed you that Soviet citizens Baselin and Bu洛維克 had been severely tortured and crippled. On October 13, he again informed you of the cruel torture suffered by Soviet citizen Osaduk. On the 15th, he informed you that Osaduk had died from excessive torture. On October 19, he again informed you that another person, Gulbaseki, had died from severe torture by border guards in Manzhouli. I have repeatedly discussed with you the fate of Soviet citizens Kislov and Panshkin and informed you of the shocking news in this case. According to reliable reports I have received, these two men also died from injuries inflicted by border police officers. Although the authorities have made unintelligent statements about this, it is only to cover up these crimes. At the same time, the authorities' strict refusal to allow representatives of the Consul-General to meet with the prisoners is sufficient to prove that torture is indeed a fact, and that the authorities are concealing these actions from the Consul-General's office. What is mentioned above does not fully describe the news of the severe torture suffered by Soviet citizens in Harbin, Suifenhe, and other places (these events are the subject of my repeated protests). Your Excellency should provide a specific answer to this and explain what measures have been taken to severely punish these criminals to prevent such incidents from recurring. However, you have not mentioned these facts at all, stating only that the authorities did not use severe torture during the interrogation. This answer only indicates that the Manchurian leaders and political organs are clearly attempting to use the authority of their highest authorities to shield police officers and military police from illegal acts of violence against Soviet people, and to give the impression that the government is encouraging these actions and not punishing them. Therefore, the highest government organs of 'Manchuria' should bear full responsibility to the Soviet government for the aforementioned acts of torture and illegality. Therefore, in my capacity as a representative of the Soviet People's Commissariat for Foreign Affairs, I dare to inform you that Your Excellency's response on November 6 to the points I applied for and protested is completely unsatisfactory. I now confirm my previous protests to the 'Manchurian' side regarding the illegal arrest and torture of Soviet citizens, and again firmly demand that all previously illegally arrested Soviet citizens be released immediately, that the torture of them be completely stopped, and that those who use torture be severely punished. Finally, I hold the 'Manchurian government' organs responsible for all the losses suffered by Soviet citizens as a result of the actions of these police officers and military police, both moral and material, and I reserve the right to demand compensation for the losses suffered by each Soviet citizen due to illegal arrest and torture, as well as for the losses of Soviet citizens Kislov,劳什金, Gulbazki, and Osaduk, who died in Manchurian prisons due to torture," etc. (TASS dispatch, 12th)

On the one hand, the starving are everywhere, while elsewhere, grain is wasted in streams. The most frustrating thing about this situation is that the countries responsible for convening the Disarmament Conference are still competing to increase armaments. Henderson therefore agreed with the proposal to organize an international police force, which should be placed under the command of the League of Nations, and said that if countries are prepared to organize a world economic association, then this organization is the first step in establishing the United States of International Nations. The American Economic Situation Shows Signs of Stabilization (American Correspondence) 99

Panic Temporarily Reduced, Businesses Gradually Recovering

Striving for Self-Improvement on the Eve of Disarmament

The central problem of the economic panic in the United States is the unemployment problem. Although there are no accurate statistics on the number of unemployed, most experts estimate that there are 11 million to 12.5 million unemployed, and about 4 million family members need to be assisted. Therefore, this is the most important problem facing the United States today. If it is properly resolved, the American economy will recover, and the capitalist organization may be re-stabilized. Therefore, in the past year and a half, this matter has been a major issue of concern to both the government and the public.

At the end of August, when President Roosevelt explained the "New Deal," he said, "The government is trying to adjust the national economy and establish the national principle of a country without an unemployed population. Now we must first study how to eliminate the existing unemployed population. Secondly, the wise countermeasures to be studied are to prevent unemployment from recurring."

These words have been said since Roosevelt took office. Now, repeating the original meaning is only a slight change in wording. In recent months, the actual number of unemployed has not only increased, but labor-capital disputes have also continued to occur. The relationships involved in the disputes are expanding more and more. The San Francisco dockworkers' strike was relatively large, and the textile workers' strike was even larger. If this continues, the entire golden world, the economic situation of the United States of America, is very worrying, because as a result of the intensification of labor-capital conflicts, no one can guarantee that accidents will not happen. Fortunately, after the textile workers' strike, the president took on the role of mediator, and a considerable solution has now been reached. There will not be a major movement in the short term.

However, the unemployment problem is still very large. Therefore, the 30-hour work week advocated by William Green, president of the American Federation of Labor, has attracted the attention of the general public. He said, "In winter, special attention should be paid to relieving the unemployed from hunger and cold, guaranteeing them a minimum standard of living, and extending a hand to provide appropriate relief to the families of the unemployed." He believes that if the working hours of workers are shortened to five hours per week, then after the current 40-hour to 45-hour per week system is changed, 1.7 million people will immediately get jobs. Labor Secretary Perkins expressed goodwill towards this opinion, but most employers disagreed. Therefore, there may still be some small problems this winter, but on the whole, it can barely pass.

According to a survey by the New York Times, the overall index of business activity in the United States (assuming its normal state is 100) was 85.1 in mid-June, 78.6 in mid-August, and as low as 71.9 in mid-September. This is similar to the situation after the financial panic in April last year. Among them, the steel industry is the most serious, with actual work only 40% of that in June this year, equivalent to 20.9% of total working capacity. The textile industry has also been affected by strikes and narrow sales channels. In early September, weekly production of cotton cloth was only 75 million square yards, which was 25.6 million square yards less than the weekly average in June and July.

However, the purchasing power of the general public increased by more than 9 million US dollars in September compared to August, and building contracts also increased by more than 1 million US dollars. Industrial stocks also rose by 78 US dollars in mid-September, and the future and hope have increased, and a glimmer of recovery has reappeared. Because of this relationship, the government authorities are bolder, and with a considerable grasp of domestic problems, they can prepare as much as possible for foreign affairs, especially to cope with the disarmament preparatory meeting to be held in October.

According to what is heard here, Japan will strongly advocate the abolition of previous naval treaties and equality of armaments. The United States will never be willing to relax on this point. It believes that the foundation of peace is based on the Washington Treaty and the London Agreement. If these two treaties are abolished, it will not be easy to establish a new treaty. After the balance of power in the Pacific is broken, a world crisis will follow, and naval competition will become more intense. Therefore, the United States must make practical preparations in diplomacy and implement its peace proposals, but in fact, it has few allies. Japan is of course directly opposed to it, and the United Kingdom does not necessarily side with the United States. In politics, it also has a similar feeling to Japan. However, after the disarmament conference breaks down, naval competition is to be expected. The American manufacturing industry, which has always been centered on business, may also inevitably shift its gears to the military industry. This kind of trace cannot be seen at present, but what will happen in the future, we can imagine. (October 10, 1934, New York)

League of Nations Water Conservancy Experts Arrive in Peiping 100

Investigating Water Conservancy Projects in North China

Leaving China in Two Months

Peiping Correspondence: The League of Nations, in response to China's request to improve China's water conservancy and river works, specially selected four experts, Goode, Cousin, Nie Youfu, and Omodeo, to come to China last month. Omodeo is a water conservancy expert, and Cousin is a highway expert. Omodeo and Cousin arrived in Shanghai last week from Italy and France respectively. The next morning, Omodeo, accompanied by his assistant Satauli, Pu Deli, consultant of the National Economic Council, and Zhang Junqi, commissioner, went north and arrived in Peiping at 10:24 AM today (the 11th), and stayed at the Beijing Hotel. Cousin has scheduled to come north tomorrow (the 12th) and will transfer from Peiping to Xi'an, follow the Xilan Highway to Lanzhou, and inspect the road project. Omodeo is scheduled to take the Peiping-Baotou express train to Suiyuan at 3:00 PM tomorrow (the 12th) and transfer to Salachi County to investigate the Minsheng Canal project. Therefore, after Omodeo arrived in Peiping today (the 11th), he went to the Hua Yang Relief Association at 2:00 PM to meet with Zhang Yuanshan, the general manager, and Tader, the chief engineer, to inquire about the construction process and engineering design of the canal in detail. Omodeo's group is scheduled to stay in Suiyuan for seven days, and then come to Peiping to meet with the two experts, Nie Youfu and Goode. Nie and Goode are currently on a sea voyage and are expected to arrive in Shanghai on the 16th of this month. They are scheduled to leave for the north on the 17th and may make a short stay when passing through Peiping. They are expected to arrive in Peiping on the 21st. Nie and Goode are both water conservancy experts. After the three gather in Peiping, they will take the same train to Tianjin to inspect the Haihe project and the Yongding River fundamental treatment project. Then they will go to Xi'an to inspect the Jingwei Canal. If time permits, they will transfer to Taiyuan. When Omodeo passed through Tianjin this morning (the 11th), he originally planned to get off the train in Tianjin and go to Kaifeng to inspect the Yellow River. Later, in order to save time, he temporarily suspended the plan and waited for Nie and Goode to come north before going to Hebei, Shandong, and Henan provinces to inspect the Yellow River together. According to the investigation, after the three experts, Omodeo, Nie, and Goode, finish inspecting the Yellow River, they will go south to inspect the Yangtze River. The round-trip time is scheduled for two months, because the four experts sent by the League of Nations this time were originally scheduled to stay in China for three months to allow them to conduct a leisurely inspection and design. Now, for some reason, it has been changed to two months, and the inspection itinerary has to be shortened. (11th)

Mining Strife Repeatedly Occurs in Tangdong 101

Majia Gou Miners Strike

Demanding the Abolition of the Contracting System

Tianjin Correspondence: More than one hundred workers on the third street of the Kailuan Majiagou mine went on strike suddenly at 1:00 PM on the 9th of this month, just as shifts were changing. After the strike, all the striking workers held wooden sticks and wore yellow armbands with the words "Oppose Petty Contracting" written on them, forming a group similar to a picket line and active in the mining area, forcing other internal and external workers to act in unison. The second security team stationed at the mine mobilized the entire team after hearing the news and guarded inside and outside the mining area, and persuaded the workers to return to work. The workers then elected five representatives to demand: (1) that the Rui Sheng Company, the contractor, abolish the petty contracting system; (2) that workers shall no longer be oppressed in the future. After the incident, the representative of Rui Sheng Company rushed to the Tangshan Mining Bureau and requested that the mining area police be informed and armed suppression be carried out. The conditions put forward by the workers were not accepted by anyone, resulting in a serious situation in the mining area. The third street mine was completely shut down. According to the workers, the reason for the occurrence of this incident was that Rui Sheng Company, the contractor, sought huge profits and contracted part of the project to petty contractors. The ninth coal mine of the third street has been contracted, and the workers believe that layer-by-layer exploitation of rights violates the contract between the mining bureau and the workers, so they expressed their opposition. A labor dispute once occurred because of this matter last month, which was later calmed down because Rui Sheng Company, the contractor, voluntarily withdrew its proposal. Now the company has resumed the previous plan, and the workers have resisted by striking. However, according to other sources, there are currently many bandits lurking in the Majiagou mining area. Such as Communist traitors, all create trouble out of nothing and provoke labor-capital struggles. Recently, the traitor Zhao Dazhong sent Guo Lantian to Dongsi Mines, including Majiagou, to secretly organize the Second Pseudo-Strong Army, inciting workers to join, and not a few have joined. Guo's Pseudo-Second Army governs three brigades, and each brigade plans to recruit three thousand people. The firearms are transported from Tanggu by a certain foreigner. All those who prove to be loyal after joining will be issued firearms. The purpose of recruitment is entirely in the mining area workers. Therefore, the mining area has long been restless. Zhao Zhuang and Majiagou have more miners and are already under martial law. This strike by the Majiagou miners is only ostensibly to fight for the exploitation of petty contracting interests, but in reality, the background is not so simple. Zhao Xun, the director of the Tangshan Public Security Bureau, has sent the inspector general to investigate and try to quell the incident. Also, the workers of the Tangshan Qixin Cement Company have always enjoyed the best treatment and there has been no labor dispute. On the 7th of this month, they suddenly used the excuse that the company charged workers a higher price for buying cement than the contractors, and thousands of workers brewed a strike. The factory learned about it in advance and secretly reported it to the security team, which sent a large team of police to guard the company. The workers saw that the news had been leaked and did not take any action. However, starting from the morning of the 8th, they implemented a go-slow. Although the workers still arrived at the company on time, they did not work. Fortunately, the company manager was quick-witted and secretly summoned the workers' leaders to conduct open and honest persuasion, and after persuading the remaining workers, they resumed work in the afternoon of the 9th. However, the mining area police are afraid that there will still be repeated incidents and have not relaxed their guard. (10th)

Jinan Cracks Down on Important Reactionary Organizations Again 102

Many Pseudo-Military Officers Captured

Jinan Correspondence: In July this autumn, disaffected military personnel, including You Renxiao, were secretly active in Jinan, contacting bandits, and attempting to cause disturbance. Their agency was located in Wangguanzhuang, south of Jinan City. They used the name of Yimin Company for activities, and determined the size of the class according to the amount of stock. You Renxiao served as the commander-in-chief, Huang Ziliang as the deputy commander, and there were pseudo-third road lieutenant general Shuzhentang, first division commander Ren Buyuan, second division commander Wang Zhongting, third division commander Liu Junming, fourth division commander Liu Yanbin, fifth division commander Bu Hanzhang, first brigade commander Zhang Huchen, second brigade commander Wang Zhizhong, third brigade commander Lv Xianbin, etc. The matter was discovered by the special detective team. On July 14th, team leader Liu Yaoting led the team to Wangguanzhuang to search and captured Shuzhentang. Huang Ziliang and others were on the run. Huang's relative, Jie Guangsong, was captured. Later, the pseudo-first brigade commander Yue Dai and pseudo-military officer Hou Zhenhuan were captured in Yuanliuzhuang. The fugitive pseudo-first brigade commander Zhang Huchen went to Tai'an to carry out activities openly, contacting lurking bandits. Feng Yuxiang's guards, together with the Tai'an County Government, captured Zhang and sent him to Jinan for trial together. Chairman Han reported to Chairman Chiang by telegram, and Chiang sent a telegram praising him and ordering him to continue the search. The reactionary elements temporarily restrained themselves slightly, and the arrested pseudo-military officers were also sentenced to permanent imprisonment.

Unexpectedly, after a few months, the reactionary elements relapsed and secretly came to Jinan again, establishing an agency at No. 14 Nanshang Street, Weiyi Road, in the commercial port, still using the name of Yimin Company and using the method of issuing invoices as proxies. The person in charge was pseudo-division commander Wang Shude. After the news leaked out, the special detective team learned about it and team deputy Feng Xiuan led team members to ambush and arrest the suspects on Shangshan Street at about 1:00 AM today (the 10th). Wang Shude was captured, and Yimin Company stocks, etc. were found. According to Wang's confession, there were still Chief of Staff Fa Ziyuan and Fa's son Fa Yi (also a pseudo-military officer) who were currently residing at Tiegong Temple by Daming Lake and were also carrying out activities. The special detective team then mobilized again and captured Fa and his son. Later, Fa confessed that Wang Zhenqiu on Yongqing Street was the representative of Commander-in-Chief You Renxiao, so they continued to search and arrest him. Wang was also captured, as well as another representative, Ding Jüzheng, and Wu Huchen, the recruitment commissioner appointed by pseudo-division commander Wang Shude, were captured at Wang Zhenqiu's home. According to Wang Zhenqiu, there were several other people who had just gone out for a walk, etc. The detective team sent 1,000 criminals to the military law department. This morning, detective team members continued to capture two pseudo-military officers, Sun Chuanxiang and Kang Youtian, at the New Market, who were also their remnants. There was also a pseudo-representative named Ren Tian (from Hejian) who had just returned home, so he escaped. The newly captured criminals were sent to the military law department in the afternoon. According to their confession, the party members active in Jinan have been wiped out in one fell swoop. (10th)

Situation of Chao-Shan News Industry 103

Strict News, Postal and Telegraphic Censorship

Shantou Correspondence: The Southwest Committee members previously issued a telegram announcing freedom of speech, abolishing the news censorship office composed of military, political, party and police personnel, and establishing a publication review committee to send personnel to guide speech. Based on this, the Shantou Journalists Association submitted a request to the Southwest Political Committee to stop various agencies from forcibly soliciting news drafts and sources from newspapers, and that original manuscripts should not be reviewed unless based on legal procedures. One month after the submission, no reply has been received, and Shantou's newspapers still have to send the original manuscripts to the censorship committee every night for stamping before they can be published. A few days ago, the New Lingdong Daily was fined to suspend publication for seven days because one news item was published without being stamped by the committee. Meixian Daily News also published a news item "Five Manifestations Temple Doing Plays", and the reporter of the newspaper was arrested by the armed forces of the training office, and was acquitted after publishing an apology. Chao'an Yongbao and New Construction Daily were severely warned by the Chao'an County Party Department for publishing Cai Fanghua's submission, claiming that the newspaper was disparaging the party's authority. Also, postal inspection is also extremely strict. News telegrams must be reviewed and stamped by the inspector before they can be sent. The inspector is not permanently stationed at the telegraph office, so news telegrams are often delayed. In the event of major news, the inspector must consult the competent officials. If the source of the news is asked, the telegrapher must be responsible for answering in detail. Therefore, the Shantou news industry is extremely hopeful that freedom of speech will be realized as soon as possible to avoid all kinds of suffering.

Songjiang

Opium Addicts Abroad Allowed to Apply for Licenses 104

The Provincial Anti-Opium Committee, considering that the registration of opium addicts has long been closed, but opium smokers often underreport or use aliases to cover up during registration, or those who have returned from abroad have no way to apply for supplementary licenses, it is inevitable, in order to be considerate of opium addicts, it is specially accommodated, and all county anti-opium committees are ordered to allow opium addicts who have returned from abroad to apply for supplementary registration and issue licenses with the certification of the township head. Those who are not laborers but obtain type B licenses by deception are allowed to exchange them for type A licenses, those who report insufficient consumption are allowed to increase the amount, and those who use aliases are also allowed to correct them, otherwise, once found in the future, they will be severely punished according to the law, etc. The County Anti-Opium Committee has ordered the district chiefs of each district to convey the message to the township head for effective publicity.

Wuxi

The East Gate Ice Factory Suddenly Suffers a Mishap

There is a Wuxi Ice Factory outside the East Gate of this county, in front of the Taying Bridge, which was established by Wang Jingui and others by raising funds, and the business is very good. The factory has two ice ponds, covering an area of about ten mu. The factory buildings are all built of rice straw and bamboo. Yesterday (the 11th) at about 9:00 PM, due to carelessness with fire, it suddenly burned down. Residents nearby immediately rang the gongs to sound the alarm, and fire brigades from all sections rushed to the scene to rescue the fire. After more than an hour, it was extinguished, burning one ice pond and causing a loss of about 2,000 yuan.

Opium Pill Offender Executed by Firing Squad 105

The Public Security First Branch discovered Shen Tingshi, a person who set up a hall to provide people with red pills for smoking, in a thatched shed in Ximen Rihui Lane on August 21 of this year (43 years old, from Wuxi, formerly a peddler). He was transferred to the county government and then transferred to the Zhenjiang Garrison Headquarters for review. After strict interrogation by the headquarters, it was confirmed that the offender had repeatedly committed the crime of setting up a place to provide people with highly addictive drugs for smoking, and his crime was unforgivable. He was sentenced to death and submitted to the Nanchang Camp for approval. At about 9:00 PM the night before, the order was sent back to the county government of this county for execution. Yesterday (the 12th) at 3:00 PM, the county clerk Yu signed and brought Shen Ting to the court for interrogation, and then escorted him to the South School Field for execution by firing squad.

Police-Merchant Corps Conflict, Shops Close 106

Jin Bingchun, the acting patrol officer of the Anzhen Eighth Resident Station, learned that gambling was rampant in Donghutang Town. On the day before yesterday at 1:00 PM, he personally led nine police officers to arrest them. He first went to Wang Helin's teahouse, and then to Zhou San's teahouse to search, and arrested nine gamblers. Just as he was about to take them away, many villagers and members of the 22nd Detachment of the Merchant Corps surrounded Patrol Officer Jin and the police officers, robbed the gamblers, and fired four or five shots as a demonstration. The police officers immediately fired back. For a time, gunshots crackled, as if facing a formidable enemy. As a result, a stray bullet injured the leg of police officer Su Sanshi. Later, he was rescued by the 3rd squadron of the Security Team. The shops in the town were closed one after another, and the situation expanded. Patrol Officer Jin reported the situation to the main examiner and sent the injured police officer to the city for treatment. After receiving the report, Director Chen immediately sent Inspector Wang to lead forty officers from the guard and patrol teams to go down to the countryside to suppress the situation and investigate the truth of the incident. He also persuaded the shops to open and hunted down the gamblers for legal action.

Changzhou

Robbery Occurs Inside Zhongshan Gate 107

At about 1:00 PM on the 11th, Li Chengyuan, a traveler, arrived at the Chunxing Inn near the Wuyi Railway Station and then opened Room No. 7 to rest. Li was a salesman from the Jiading Daxing Woolen Mill. He came to Chang from Danyang on this day, carrying a large number of towels, preparing to sell them to various stores. At about 7:00 PM in the evening, a person suddenly came to the inn to visit Li, saying that the store needed to buy towels. Li accompanied him into the city, and when he arrived at the Dongshantou place inside the Land Temple in Zhongshan, another person suddenly came and blocked the way, and took out a pistol to scare him into silence. Then he used a rope to tie his hands behind his back, tightly covering his eyes with his belt. Then he robbed him of 400 yuan in cash and more than 60 yuan in cash and miscellaneous items from his body. Afterwards, Li Chengyuan rushed to the Yingchun Bridge to report to the police on duty to pursue the robbers, but the robbers had already escaped. The public security organs paid great attention to the occurrence of a robbery in the city, and searched and investigated everywhere late at night, and inquired at various hotels, but found nothing.

Zhenjiang

Notable Arrest of Local Opium Dealer Sun Yanwu 108

The Provincial Anti-Opium Committee, acting on a confidential report, learned that a well-known Yangzhou opium dealer named Sun Yanwu and others were establishing an organization to secretly traffic in illicit opium. Upon receiving the report, the committee dispatched Ling Xixian to Yangzhou, where he coordinated with the Jiangdu County Anti-Opium Association. In the Dayuan area, Sun Yanwu was arrested, and eight packages of opium and numerous opium paraphernalia were seized. In addition, a suspected opium dealer named Zeng Zhang was apprehended in Lantern Lane, East Circle Gate, along with three blocks of opium. The suspects were taken to the county for interrogation. Subsequently, police officers escorted the opium suspects Sun Yanwu, Liu Chenshi, and two others by car to the provincial capital, where they were transferred to the Zhenjiang Garrison Command for interrogation and legal proceedings.

Haimen

Sampan Operators Petition for Resumption of Business 109

Due to the overloading of passengers, sampans in various ports of this county have repeatedly caused accidents. The county chamber of commerce, with the approval of the county government, ordered them to cease operations. However, the sampan operators in various ports, totaling over two hundred people, have faced financial difficulties and are on the brink of starvation since losing their jobs. Yesterday (the 10th), all sampan operators gathered and came to the county to petition the county party headquarters and the county government, requesting permission to resume business in order to make a living. Li, a standing committee member of the county party headquarters, and Hu, the secretary of the county government, received them and persuaded them to return home and await a suitable solution. The sampan operators were satisfied and left.

Local News

Shanghai Press Wires Fifth Plenary Session 110

Respectful Admiration for Telegram from Wang and Chiang

Two Requests Made

The Shanghai Newspaper Association and the Shanghai Journalists Association separately wired the Fifth Plenary Session yesterday, expressing admiration for the telegram from Wang and Chiang, and making two requests. The full text of the telegrams is transcribed below:

Telegram from the Newspaper Association 111

To the Presidium of the Fifth Plenary Session in Nanjing: The opening of the plenary session has brought joy to the entire nation. Having read the telegram from Mr. Wang and Mr. Chiang, which enumerates five points on the path to national salvation and good governance, and the means of peaceful unification, we deeply admire and respect them as essential plans for saving the times. In particular, the item on safeguarding freedom of speech is something our association has long aspired to. We believe that in the past, when the Red bandits were rampant and the national army launched a large-scale campaign of suppression, the order of the rear should be sought for stability, and the legal freedom of speech and association of the people was inevitably restricted to some extent. Fortunately, Chairman Chiang's supervision of the suppression has been victorious, and there are no traces of bandits in Fujian and Jiangxi. The peaceful unification of the country has also been realized. It seems appropriate to lift the aforementioned provisional measures restricting freedom, in order to conform to the sincere intention of Mr. Wang and Mr. Chiang to respect the freedom of the people. Now that all the members of the Central Committee are gathered in the capital to discuss national affairs, this association respectfully appeals to your council to adopt and implement the following two matters first: (1) Before the system of news censorship is abolished, we request that you issue a general order to the news censorship offices in various regions, urging them to strictly abide by the censorship standards set by the central government, handle matters with care, and avoid being overly harsh, so as to avoid discrepancies. (2) News organizations that have been punished in the past, but are not backed by force or riots, should be generously restored to their former status in order to observe their future behavior. We humbly express our sincerity and respectfully request your clear consideration. Shanghai Newspaper Association. (Printed matter)

Telegram from the Journalists Association 112

To the Presidium of the Fifth Plenary Session in Nanjing: The national telegram from Mr. Wang and Mr. Chiang advocates that the people and social organizations should enjoy freedom of speech and association in accordance with the law, but if they are not backed by force or riots, the government must guarantee and not prevent them. After reading it, we are filled with admiration. We have learned that in recent years, due to the rampant Red bandits and the unstable domestic order, the government has had no choice but to impose restrictions on the legal freedom of the people. Fortunately, the bandits have been completely suppressed in Fujian and Jiangxi, and the unity of the country has been achieved. The provisional measures restricting freedom of speech can gradually be lifted, so that the people's thoughts can be freely developed, in line with the spirit of political tutelage and education. According to news from Beijing, the proposals of Mr. Wang and Mr. Chiang have been adopted by your council and handed over to the Central Political Committee for implementation, which is deeply gratifying. Based on the spirit of the telegram from Mr. Wang and Mr. Chiang, this association appeals to your council: (1) Before the news censorship system is abolished, it is necessary to strictly order all regions to strictly abide by the standards set by the central government and handle matters with care, avoiding being overly harsh, so as to avoid discrepancies. (2) News organizations that have been punished, if they are not definitely backed by force or riots, should be immediately restored to their former status to show leniency. We urgently hope that the above two items will be adopted and implemented first, and we cannot help but look forward to it. Shanghai Journalists Association. (Printed matter)

Germany Bans Remittances from Chinese Merchants

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Telegraphed Yesterday Requesting Negotiations 117

Please Request the German Ambassador to Negotiate and Lift the Ban in Accordance with the Sino-German Treaty

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Foreign Affairs yesterday, stating, "To the Nanjing Ministry of Foreign Affairs: On the 11th of this month, we received a letter from the Yantai District Hairnet and Lace Industry Association of Fushan County, Shandong, stating that the hairnets, lace, embroidery, and other goods produced in Yantai are related to the livelihoods of the poor and foreign trade. Since they have been exported to Europe and the United States, there have never been any difficulties. Now, the German government is restricting remittances, which is unexpected. The import tax on lace, embroidery, and other goods shipped to Germany was previously levied on each kilo according to weight at 7.5 German marks. Now, it has increased to 30 German marks per kilo. Based on the value of the goods, the tax is approximately 130 marks per 100 marks worth of goods. With such a heavy tax, business has suffered a great loss. Unexpectedly, Germany is also restricting remittances. In the past few months, each person was allowed to remit about 5,000 yuan per month, which has gradually been reduced to 200 yuan. Now, it is completely prohibited. Although there are large sums of money accumulated, not a single cent can be remitted, causing Chinese merchants to be trapped and unable to move, no different from being sentenced to death. It is believed that the goods in your area that are shipped to Germany must also be suffering the same pain, and we fear that merchants across the country will be directly or indirectly affected. It is understood that trade between countries is based on the principle of mutual benefit. As for the Sino-German relationship, it has always been harmonious and should be of equal benefit. Our country allows German goods to be imported as much as possible and German merchants to remit large sums of money at their convenience. Now, Germany has suddenly restricted remittances from Chinese merchants, which is extremely unfair. If we allow them to treat us harshly at will, what can we expect for the future of foreign trade? Our association is unable to do anything on its own. We can only rely on your help to respond to each other. In addition to submitting a request to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, we hereby request your esteemed association to verify and assist us and proceed together. Please promptly request the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate in order to maintain international trade. We would be most grateful."

Flying from Hangzhou to Shanghai to Beijing This Morning

Two Notices from the Jianghai Customs 119

Wireless Radio Materials Require Transit Permits

Limits on the Number of Silver Dollars Carried by Passengers

Notice One 120

Tang Hai'an, the Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, and Bolade, the Tax Commissioner, issued a notice yesterday regarding wireless radio materials, whether in transit or re-exported, requiring a transit permit before being released. The notice, numbered 1407, read: "According to Order No. 9536 of the Ministry of Finance, wireless radio materials and equipment reported for transit should be applied for transit permits from the local telegraph bureau. However, those related to military use will be issued by the Ministry of Communications. This should be followed. Hereafter, all reports of the aforementioned items, whether for transit or re-export, will be released with a transit permit; otherwise, the goods will be detained immediately. If the permit is not presented after a long period of time, it will be confiscated. All merchants, please be informed."

Notice Two 121

Tang Hai'an, the Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, and Bolade, the Tax Commissioner, issued a notice yesterday regarding the number of silver dollars passengers traveling to and from domestic ports are allowed to carry, in accordance with the order. The notice, numbered 1408, read: "Now, in accordance with the order of the Ministry of Finance, the number of silver dollars passengers traveling to and from domestic ports are allowed to carry shall not exceed one thousand yuan. If this number is exceeded, the entire amount will be confiscated. All merchants and people, please be informed."

Four French Warships

Sailed to Zhejiang Waters Yesterday for Artillery Practice 122

Scheduled to Sail to Ningbo for Tourism Today

French Consul-General Telegraphed Zhejiang Provincial Government for Verification

The Xinxin News Agency reported that four French warships stationed in Shanghai sailed from Shanghai to the waters off Qiliyu Island outside Zhenhai Port on the morning of the 12th (yesterday) to test their artillery. They are scheduled to sail to Ningbo for tourism on the 13th (today). The French Consul-General in Shanghai, Meili, telegraphed the Zhejiang Provincial Government to inform its subordinates and the public to avoid misunderstandings. It is reported that the Zhejiang Provincial Government has instructed the Zhenhai County Magistrate, Artillery Commander, Water Police, Public Security Bureau, and other agencies to verify. The original text read: "Recently, we received a telegram from French Consul-General Meili stating that the French warships CarnnrFranin, etc., will test their artillery in the waters of Zhenhai on the 12th of this month and will travel to Ningbo on the 13th. Please inform the people to avoid misunderstandings."

Your association should verify and provide assistance to conduct a unified process. Speedily petition the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for negotiations in order to maintain international trade. We are extremely grateful. We found two items in the information sent by the association. First, the issue of high taxes on Chinese goods, according to Article 4 of the Sino-German Treaty and Article 1, Paragraph 2 of the Sino-German Supplementary Treaty of 1928, the taxes on goods imported and exported by the two countries shall not be higher or different from the taxes paid by the people of this country or any other country. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs should investigate whether Germany taxes the same goods produced in this country or other countries at a rate as high as 130 out of 100. This will be used to prepare for negotiations. Second, the issue of banning remittances from Chinese merchants is tantamount to banning Chinese people from doing business in Germany, which is inconsistent with Article 3 of the Sino-German Treaty, which states that the people of this country have the right to engage in commerce or industry in the territory of the other country. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs should telegraph the ambassador to Germany to conduct thorough negotiations and lift the ban or restore the previous system of limiting remittances to 5,000 yuan per month. Furthermore, according to Article 2 of the Sino-German Supplementary Treaty of 1928, the two contracting countries should begin negotiations on a treaty of commerce and navigation in the shortest possible time, based on the principle of complete uniformity and equal treatment. It has been nearly seven years since then, but no work has been started on this matter. As a result, when commercial issues are encountered, applying treaty text cannot achieve a comprehensive response. Please also check the old cases and quickly begin negotiations for the sake of public convenience. Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce. Zhen.

The Ministry of Finance Telegraphed a Reply to the General Chamber of Commerce

Approval to Waive Inland Grain Tax 123

Executive Yuan Replied to Reduce Yangtze River Shipping Rates by Half

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of the Republic of China previously approved a telegram from the Chongqing Chamber of Commerce on behalf of the people, stating that given the drought in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, it would be better to purchase and transport stored grain from Sichuan rather than purchasing foreign rice. It also requested that the Sichuan and Zhejiang authorities be telegraphed to exempt grain from inland taxes and that all ships on the Yangtze River reduce shipping rates. The association telegraphed the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance on September 3 to handle the matter. Replies have now been received, which are recorded separately as follows:

The Ministry of Finance Telegraphed Approval to Waive Inland Grain Tax 124

The association received a reply telegram from the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating, "To the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce: According to the previous telegram from the Jiangxi representative of the association, requesting that Sichuan and Hunan provinces be ordered to waive inland grain taxes, we have already ordered the finance departments of Sichuan, Hunan, and Hubei provinces to investigate and handle the matter and have issued instructions in each case. According to the Hubei Finance Department's report of November 19, 1934, 'We received Order No. 8386 from the Ministry of Finance, ordering us to forward to the provincial government for transmission to be followed by the county government. In addition to issuing orders to each business tax bureau to comply, we have combined the report of compliance for review.' Based on this, since the Hubei Provincial Government has ordered its subordinates to comply with the exemption of inland grain taxes, it can be smoothly implemented. In addition to instructions, we hereby send a telegram to inform you and ask that you forward it to the Chongqing Chamber of Commerce. Ministry of Finance Yang Fu Yin."

Yangtze River Shipping Rates Reduced by Half 125

At the same time, the association received a reply from the Secretariat of the Executive Yuan, stating, "According to your previous telegram of September 23, requesting that the authorities of Sichuan and Hunan provinces exempt inland grain taxes and order all ships on the Yangtze River to reduce shipping rates in order to resist foreign rice and circulate stored grain, this matter was transferred to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Communications. According to the Ministry of Communications' reply, 'We have copied the original telegram and sent it to the state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association for discussion. According to the company's report, "Previously, this case was proposed by our company for discussion by various industries in Shanghai. It was proposed to collect all export grain freight rates at half price. The various industries did not agree, making it difficult to implement. We previously telegraphed your ministry and will report again after the reduction method is agreed upon. As years have passed, the opinions of the industries have not been unified, and the domestic agricultural and commercial depression is becoming more and more evident. Shipping companies believe that the import and export of goods from various places are not smooth, there are few goods, and competition is becoming more intense. In the past six months, all freight rates have been reduced without exception, especially for grain. As a result, shipping costs are increasing day by day, while freight rates are decreasing. For example, for grain, freight rates have been secretly reduced again and again. According to the current situation, they have indeed been reduced to the lowest level. The revenue from freight is only enough to cover labor costs and there is no profit to be made. If freight rates are reduced again according to the current price, not only will the opinions of the industries fail to be unified, but our company's shipping costs will be difficult to maintain. Therefore, it is difficult to comply with the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce's request to reduce freight rates on the Yangtze River. The circumstances are unavoidable, and we ask for your understanding." The Ministry of Communications also stated, "We have issued orders to each member of the Yangtze River route, and have determined to collect half of the freight charge to the regulationed price for a test period of six months." We have replied with a special note for the price of grain transportation in various ports. Please send your reference to the Ministry of Communications for review and recovery."

Detailed Figures for Yangtze River Shipping Rates 126

The reporter from the Guowen News Agency specifically investigated and obtained detailed figures for grain freight rates from various ports from the shipping industry yesterday. Yichang to Shanghai is 7.75 cents (per 100 kg unit). Shashi to Shanghai is 4.6 cents. Xiangtan to Shanghai is 5.5 cents. Hankou to Shanghai is 4.66 cents. Jiujiang to Shanghai is 3.06 cents. Wuhu to Shanghai is 2.98 cents. Nanjing to Shanghai is 2.25 cents. Zhenjiang to Shanghai is 2.85 cents.

Xiang He and British Merchants Sign Antimony Ore Contract

Japanese Ambassador Lodges Protest with Our Ministry of Foreign Affairs 134

Sending Orders to Suma in Beijing to Raise with the Ministry

British Merchants Unwilling to Express Anything

A dispatch from the Zhonglian News Agency in this city reported that the British firm, Jardine, Matheson & Co., has recently signed a contract with the Hunan Provincial Government regarding the exclusive sale of Hunan antimony ore. The Japanese side, using the excuse that the British firm is monopolizing the rights to the antimony ore, had the Japanese consul in Changsha lodge a protest with the Hunan Provincial Government Chairman on the 4th of this month, which was rejected by Chairman He. It is now reported that the Japanese Ambassador Arima suddenly lodged a formal protest with our Ministry of Foreign Affairs yesterday, claiming that the contract violates the Open Door Policy and the Sino-Japanese Treaty of Commerce, intending to interfere with our normal commercial activities. This is extremely absurd. The Zhonglian News Agency reporter investigated the details as follows:

Protest Lodged Yesterday 135

Japanese Ambassador Arima sent a protest document to the resident consulate in Beijing yesterday afternoon, ordering the Japanese authorities to lodge the protest. This morning, the Japanese Embassy formally announced the contents of the protest document, stating that the British firm Jardine, Matheson & Co. has obtained the exclusive sales rights to Hunan antimony ore, which is tantamount to monopolizing the rights and is contrary to Articles 9 and 15 of the Sino-Japanese Treaty of Commerce.

Jardine, Matheson & Co. Expresses 136

The Zhonglian News Agency reporter went to the British firm Jardine, Matheson & Co. on Museum Road yesterday afternoon and met with Manager Morris, asking about the firm's contract with Hunan Province for the exclusive sale of Hunan antimony ore. He replied that it was true and that it had already been signed, but he was unwilling to express anything.

Japanese Coveting Hunan Antimony 137

The amount of antimony ore produced in Hunan Province is about 5 million tons per year, accounting for about 80% of the world's total production. Antimony ore is an essential raw material for modern industry, such as the manufacture of copper-iron machinery, which requires antimony ore. Therefore, the price is extremely high. During the European War, the market price was 3,000 yuan per ton. The current market price is still around 500 yuan. Because Japan has no antimony ore production, its antimony ore needs to be supplied by China. Therefore, it has been coveting the large amount of antimony produced in Hunan for a long time.

Announces Suspension of Business for Reorganization 140

Failure to Raise Sufficient Capital Causes Financial Difficulties

According to Xin Xin News Agency, the Wing On Silver Company, located at 473 North Sichuan Road, was established on September 3 of this year, registered with the US government, with a total capital of 500,000 yuan, of which only over 200,000 yuan was actually raised. It is found that since the opening of the company, the total amount of deposits received is about 60,000 to 70,000 yuan, and the amount of loans issued is also 80,000 to 90,000 yuan. The income and expenses are more than balanced, so there is no major problem for depositors. According to Xin Xin News Agency reporters, some shareholders have decided to reorganize, planning to add 200,000 yuan of capital, reduce the scope of business, and continue operations. The shareholders are currently exchanging opinions and negotiating.

Page 11

Garrison Headquarters

Executed Morphine Manufacturers Yesterday Morning 143

Zhang Jinbiao from Ningbo, Han Bangjie from Shaoxing

According to the Central News Agency, in early August this year, the reconnaissance team of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters cracked down on a morphine manufacturing organization inside a foreigner's garden on Hongqiao Road, arrested the car driver Ge Rongrui, and seized manufacturing equipment and chemicals. The principal offender, Zhang Zongguo, also known as Zhang Jinbiao, escaped through the back door. Later, in early October, the Detective Team of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau learned that Zhang Jinbiao and others had set up a factory to manufacture morphine in the Hongkang Soap Factory at 21 Binggangli, Tianbao Road, Zhabei, and set up a Hongkang Soap Factory wholesale office at 2-6 Linping Road to secretly sell morphine. Members were dispatched with the police to arrest the morphine factory owner Zhang Jinbiao, engineer Han Bangjie, wholesale office bookkeeper Zhang Kebei, and six suspects including Shen Xiaoliang. More than one hundred pieces of manufacturing machinery, chemicals, and morphine raw materials were seized. They were successively handed over to the Garrison Headquarters for concurrent investigation. It is learned that after repeated interrogations by the Military Law Department of the Headquarters, Zhang Jinbiao and Han Bangjie were found to have jointly manufactured highly toxic drugs, and the evidence was very clear. Both were sentenced to death. Zhang Kebei was also found to have jointly sold highly toxic drugs, and he was sentenced to twelve years of imprisonment with leniency. The remaining seven people, Ge Rongrui, Shen Xiaoliang, Sun Facheng, Liu Yonggen, Ye Afu, Xue Deshan, and Wang Lifu, were either car drivers or soap factory workers and were not involved in the case. They were acquitted separately. The Headquarters then reported the case and judgment to the Nanchang Provisional Headquarters for approval. At 9:00 a.m. yesterday morning, members were dispatched to lead a platoon of military police to escort Zhang Jinbiao and Han Bangjie to the open space next to the Longhua Airport, verify their identities, and execute them by firing squad. The announcement of the Headquarters is recorded as follows: "According to the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau's report on the Zhang Jinbiao et al. morphine manufacturing case, the Department ordered the Military Law Department to investigate and judge according to law. Zhang Jinbiao and Han Bangjie jointly and continuously manufactured highly toxic drugs and were sentenced to death. The case and judgment have been reported to the Nanchang Provisional Headquarters of the Chairman of the Military Commission for approval. In addition to escorting the two criminals Zhang Jinbiao et al. to the execution ground, verifying their identities, and executing them by firing squad, in order to warn others, this announcement is hereby issued so that everyone knows. This announcement counts the executed highly toxic drug criminals Zhang Jinbiao, also known as Zhang Zongguo, 48 years old, from Ningbo; Han Bangjie, 33 years old, from Shaoxing. Wu Tiecheng, Commander Concurrently, December 12, 23rd Year of the Republic of China."

Executive Yuan Orders the Ministry of Military Affairs to Protect the Longhua Ancient Temple 144

Longhua Temple in this city was built in the Three Kingdoms period and is the first ancient temple in Jiangnan. In the past, it suffered a lot of damage due to repeated wars. After the current abbot Xingkong made vigorous efforts to renovate it, it has slightly restored its former appearance. For the sake of preserving famous historical sites, the Executive Yuan ordered the Ministry of Military Affairs to issue a ban on stationing troops and to protect it properly. The Ministry of Military Affairs' reply is now available as follows: "The local famous historical sites are of great cultural significance. The Ministry of the Interior has formulated preservation regulations and distributed them to all provinces and cities for compliance. This Ministry has issued prohibitions on stationing troops in the famous scenic spots of Beijing and West Lake in Hangzhou. The Longhua Temple in Shanghai is a famous ancient temple and should be strictly prohibited according to the case. This Ministry has issued a proclamation and requested the Shanghai Municipal Government to forward it for posting and to provide nearby protection, etc."

Proclamation of Penalties for Rape

In order to maintain humanity and rectify social morality, he issued Proclamation No. 371 yesterday afternoon and posted it at the entrance of the court. Those who commit rape jointly by two or more people shall be sentenced to life imprisonment or imprisonment for seven years or more. There are clear provisions in the criminal law. If anyone dares to commit the aforementioned crime, they must be severely punished according to law in order to maintain humanity and correct social morality. In addition to instructing the judicial police to investigate and deal with them at any time, this proclamation is hereby issued for public knowledge. All people, if they have seen or heard of anything, should report it truthfully so that it can be investigated."
